It is the main interface for external components\\n44:  * to make changes to the state of the cluster. For example, in distributed mode, an implementation of this interface\\n45:  * knows how to accept a connector configuration, may need to route it to the current leader worker for the cluster so\\n46:  * the config can be written to persistent storage, and then ensures the new connector is correctly instantiated on one\\n47:  * of the workers.\\n48:  * </p>\\n49:  * <p>\\n50:  * This class must implement all the actions that can be taken on the cluster (add/remove connectors, pause/resume tasks,\\n51:  * get state of connectors and tasks, etc). The non-Java interfaces to the cluster (REST API and CLI) are very simple\\n52:  * wrappers of the functionality provided by this interface.\\n53:  * </p>\\n54:  * <p>\\n55:  * In standalone mode, the implementation of this interface will be trivial because no coordination is needed. In that case,\\n56:  * the implementation will mainly be delegating tasks directly to other components. For example, when creating a new\\n57:  * connector in standalone mode, there is no need to persist the config and the connector and its tasks must run in the\\n58:  * same process, so the standalone herder implementation can immediately instantiate and start the connector and its\\n59:  * tasks.\\n60:  * </p>\\n61:  */\\n62: public interface Herder {\\n63: \\n64:     void start();\\n65: \\n66:     void stop();\\n67: \\n68:     /**\\n69:      * @return whether the worker is ready; i.e., it has completed all initialization and startup\\n70:      * steps such as creating internal topics, joining a cluster, etc.\\n71:      */\\n72:     boolean isReady();\\n73: \\n74:     /**\\n75:      * Check for worker health; i.e., its ability to service external requests from the user such\\n76:      * as creating, reconfiguring, and deleting connectors\\n77:      * @param callback callback to invoke once worker health is assured\\n78:      */\\n79:     void healthCheck(Callback<Void> callback);\\n80: \\n81:     /**\\n82:      * Get a list of connectors currently running in this cluster. For example, in distributed mode, an implementation of this interface\\n45:  * knows how to accept a connector configuration, may need to route it to the current leader worker for the cluster so\\n46:  * the config can be written to persistent storage, and then ensures the new connector is correctly instantiated on one\\n47:  * of the workers.\\n48:  * </p>\\n49:  * <p>\\n50:  * This class must implement all the actions that can be taken on the cluster (add/remove connectors, pause/resume tasks,\\n51:  * get state of connectors and tasks, etc).  throw e\n840:     } finally {\n841:       maybeChangeStatus(SHUTTING_DOWN, SHUTDOWN)\n842:     }\n843:   }\n844: \n845:   override def isShutdown(): Boolean = {\n846:     status == SHUTDOWN || status \"path\": \"server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/KafkaScheduler.java\",\n      \"symbol\": \"shutdown\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Java Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern in Apache Kafka\\n\\nApache Kafka implements a comprehensive service lifecycle pattern that ensures coordinated startup and shutdown of dependent services. The pattern follows the classic Startable/Stoppable paradigm where services are started in a specific order and shut down in reverse order to prevent resource conflicts.\\n\\n### Core Lifecycle Interfaces\\n\\nThe pattern is defined through several key interfaces:\\n\\n1. **Scheduler Interface** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java): Defines the basic lifecycle contract with `startup()` and `shutdown()` methods. This interface controls a job scheduler that allows scheduling repeating background jobs or delayed one-time actions.\\n\\n2. **ShareCoordinator Interface** (share-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/share/ShareCoordinator.java): Defines lifecycle methods `startup(IntSupplier)` and `shutdown()` for managing share group state coordination.\\n\\n3. **GroupCoordinator Interface** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinator.java): Defines lifecycle methods `startup(IntSupplier)` and `shutdown()` for managing consumer group coordination.\\n\\n4. **Herder Interface** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Herder.java): Defines lifecycle methods `start()` and `stop()` for Kafka Connect workers managing connectors and tasks.\\n\\n5. **Backing Store Interfaces**: StatusBackingStore, ConfigBackingStore, and OffsetBackingStore (connect/storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/) all follow the pattern with `start()` and `stop()` methods.\\n\\n### Service Implementations\\n\\nServices implement these interfaces:\\n\\n1. **KafkaScheduler** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/KafkaScheduler.java): Implements Scheduler with a ScheduledThreadPoolExecutor that manages scheduled tasks. Startup creates the executor, shutdown terminates it.\\n\\n2. **ShareCoordinatorService** (share-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/share/ShareCoordinatorService.java): Uses AtomicBoolean isActive flag to manage lifecycle, startup sets partition count and enables periodic jobs, shutdown reverses the process.\\n\\n3. **GroupCoordinatorService** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorService.java): Similar pattern with AtomicBoolean for state management, startup initializes coordinator runtime, shutdown closes it.\\n\\n4. **TransactionCoordinator** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/coordinator/transaction/TransactionCoordinator.scala): Exemplifies the reverse-order shutdown pattern perfectly. Startup order: scheduler.startup() → txnManager.startup() → txnMarkerChannelManager.start(). Shutdown order (line 1080-1087): scheduler.shutdown() → txnManager.shutdown() → txnMarkerChannelManager.shutdown().\\n\\n### Service Orchestration in BrokerServer\\n\\nThe **BrokerServer** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala) serves as the primary orchestrator of the service lifecycle. It manages:\\n\\n**Startup Sequence** (lines 250-599):\\n- Initializes kafkaScheduler\\n- Creates groupConfigManager and groupCoordinator\\n- Creates shareCoordinator\\n- Creates transactionCoordinator\\n- Starts alterPartitionManager\\n- Starts clientToControllerChannelManager\\n- Initializes lifecycleManager\\n- Installs metadata publishers\\n- Waits for synchronization gates using FutureUtils.waitWithLogging\\n\\n**Shutdown Sequence** (lines 729-843):\\n- Handles controlled shutdown with replicaManager and lifecycleManager\\n- Stops socket server request processing\\n- Removes metadata publishers\\n- **Shuts down kafkaScheduler early** (line 778) - critical to prevent race conditions\\n- Shuts down transactionCoordinator (line 782)\\n- Closes groupConfigManager and groupCoordinator (lines 784-789)\\n- Closes shareCoordinator (line 789)\\n- Shuts down replicaManager, alterPartitionManager, forwardingManager\\n- Closes logManager and quota managers\\n- Finally shuts down socketServer\\n\\n### Key Pattern Characteristics\\n\\n1. **Atomic State Management**: Services use AtomicBoolean flags (e.g., isActive in coordinators) for thread-safe lifecycle state tracking.\\n\\n2. **Reverse-Order Shutdown**: The TransactionCoordinator (lines 1061-1087) explicitly documents this pattern: \\\"Ordering of actions should be reversed from the startup process.\\\"\\n\\n3. **Graceful Degradation**: The BrokerServer uses CoreUtils.swallow() to catch exceptions during shutdown, ensuring all services attempt shutdown even if one fails.\\n\\n4. **Dependency Management**: BrokerLifecycleManager (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerLifecycleManager.scala) manages state transitions and controlled shutdown, coordinating with the replicaManager.\\n\\n5. **Synchronization Gates**: BrokerServer uses FutureUtils.waitWithLogging to synchronize startup phases, ensuring dependencies are ready before dependent services start.\\n\\nThis pattern ensures that when Kafka shuts down, dependent services are not cut off prematurely, preventing data loss and resource leaks. in Apache Kafka\\n\\nApache Kafka implements a comprehensive service lifecycle pattern that ensures coordinated startup and shutdown of dependent services. The pattern follows the classic Startable/Stoppable paradigm where services are started in a specific order and shut down in reverse order to prevent resource conflicts.\\n\\n### Core Lifecycle Interfaces\\n\\nThe pattern is defined through several key interfaces:\\n\\n1. **Scheduler Interface** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java): Defines the basic lifecycle contract with `startup()` and `shutdown()` methods. This interface controls a job scheduler that allows scheduling repeating background jobs or delayed one-time actions.\\n\\n2. **ShareCoordinator Interface** (share-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/share/ShareCoordinator.java): Defines lifecycle methods `startup(IntSupplier)` and `shutdown()` for managing share group state coordination.\\n\\n3. **GroupCoordinator Interface** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinator.java): Defines lifecycle methods `startup(IntSupplier)` and `shutdown()` for managing consumer group coordination.\\n\\n4. **Herder Interface** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Herder.java): Defines lifecycle methods `start()` and `stop()` for Kafka Connect workers managing connectors and tasks.\\n\\n5. **Backing Store Interfaces**: StatusBackingStore, ConfigBackingStore, and OffsetBackingStore (connect/storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/) all follow the pattern with `start()` and `stop()` methods.\\n\\n### Service Implementations\\n\\nServices implement these interfaces:\\n\\n1. **KafkaScheduler** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/KafkaScheduler.java): Implements Scheduler with a ScheduledThreadPoolExecutor that manages scheduled tasks. Startup creates the executor, shutdown terminates it.\\n\\n2. **ShareCoordinatorService** (share-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/share/ShareCoordinatorService.java): Uses AtomicBoolean isActive flag to manage lifecycle, startup sets partition count and enables periodic jobs, shutdown reverses the process.\\n\\n3. **GroupCoordinatorService** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorService.java): Similar pattern with AtomicBoolean for state management, startup initializes coordinator runtime, shutdown closes it.\\n\\n4. **TransactionCoordinator** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/coordinator/transaction/TransactionCoordinator.scala): Exemplifies the reverse-order shutdown pattern perfectly. Startup order: scheduler.startup() → txnManager.startup() → txnMarkerChannelManager.start(). Shutdown order (line 1080-1087): scheduler.shutdown() → txnManager.shutdown() → txnMarkerChannelManager.shutdown().\\n\\n### Service Orchestration in BrokerServer\\n\\nThe **BrokerServer** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala) serves as the primary orchestrator of the service lifecycle. It manages:\\n\\n**Startup Sequence** (lines 250-599):\\n- Initializes kafkaScheduler\\n- Creates groupConfigManager and groupCoordinator\\n- Creates shareCoordinator\\n- Creates transactionCoordinator\\n- Starts alterPartitionManager\\n- Starts clientToControllerChannelManager\\n- Initializes lifecycleManager\\n- Installs metadata publishers\\n- Waits for synchronization gates using FutureUtils.waitWithLogging\\n\\n**Shutdown Sequence** (lines 729-843):\\n- Handles controlled shutdown with replicaManager and lifecycleManager\\n- Stops socket server request processing\\n- Removes metadata publishers\\n- **Shuts down kafkaScheduler early** (line 778) -
